WELL EVALUATION
WELL EVALUATION
Oxy USA, Inc.
William Sadowsky 8-4-9H-142-96
Figure 1. Nabors X-20 at the Oxy USA, Inc. William Sadowksy 8-4-9H-142-96 well on January 21, 2015; 5 miles Southwest of
Manning in Dunn County, ND. (Photo by B. Lutz, Payzone Geologist)
INTRODUCTION
The Oxy USA, Inc. William Sadowsky 8-4-9H-142-96 [SESE Sec 8 , T142N, R96W] is located
approximately 5 miles Southwest of Manning, North Dakota. The subject well was drilled in Dunn County,
ND by the Nabors X-20 rig in the Manning Field of the Bakken pool. The subject well was planned with
one approximately 9,364' [Landing point to projected total depth (TD)] long southerly lateral bore with
intent to intersect regional hydraulic fracture trends that might enhance reservoir quality within the Middle
Bakken. OXY USA intends to develop oil production in the late Devonian Middle Bakken target porosity
zone with a stratigraphy consisting of siltstone, silty sandstone and limestone with depositional lithofacies
ranging from onshore terrestrial to offshore marine deposits.
ENGINEERING
Surface, Vertical & Curve Operations:
A 9 " surface hole was drilled on December 22, 2014 by a spud rig and surface casing was set
at 2,189'. The vertical hole operations commenced on December 24, 2014 with Weatherford providing
equipment and personnel for MWD and directional drilling services. The first vertical Bottom Hole
Assembly (BHA), consisting of MWD tools, 1.50° bend Hunting 7/8 5.7 motor and Tercel MR616M PDC
bit (6x16 jets), drilled to a depth of 7,568' measured depth (MD) and was pulled out due to low rates of
penetration (ROP). The second BHA had a Smith MDSi616BPX bit and a new motor. This BHA reached
a kick-off point (KOP) of 10,045' MD.
The first curve BHA (BHA #4 overall) consisted of a 2.38º bend NOV 7/8 5.0 motor, 8 ¾" Security
SKI516DP-2B PDC bit, and new MWD tools. This BHA reached curve TD 10,915` MD (~10,520' TVD)
placing the well bore approximately 6' into a 19' thick (shale to shale) Middle Bakken zone, and just
above the top of a 7' thick silty sandstone target interval. This BHA drilled the 12°/100', 870' long curve in
25 cumulative hours.
Directional tools were then pulled out of the hole and a string of 7" intermediate casing was run,
set, and cemented at a depth of 10,900' MD. The rig was then skid to William Sadowsky 7-4-9H-142-96
for vertical/curve operations. The hole was wire-lined by GYRO Data to decrease collision control
ellipsoids. Lateral operations continued on January 16th, 2015. Diesel invert drilling fluid was used
throughout the vertical hole and curve build sections maintaining a 9.8-10.1 ppg mud weight for stable
downhole conditions.
Lateral Operations:
Weatherford again provided equipment and personnel for MWD and directional drilling services.
The directional drillers, MWD hands, and Payzone geologists worked closely together throughout the
project to make steering decisions. The Inc Sonde tool was paramount in successful steering, especially
during sections where distinct gamma markers were absent.
A 6" Security MMD54 PDC bit, 1.50º Hunting mud motor, and MWD tools comprised the first
lateral BHA (5th BHA overall) and was run in the hole on 4" drill pipe starting at 10,915' MD. This BHA
drilled to a depth of 12,710' MD and the Lower Bakken Shale was encountered. The first sidetrack
location was chosen for 12,150' MD. At 17,888' MD, the BHA experienced a motor failure and was pulled
out. Once at the surface, it was observed that the bit had been lost down hole, and a second sidetrack
was scouted at 16,850' MD. When tripping back in with a new bit/motor (BHA #6) of the same model, the
fish was encountered at ~15,500' MD. The second sidetrack location was then time-drilled at 15,340' MD.
Once rotation began, it was realized that the bit had been damaged. BHA #6 was then pulled from a
depth of 15,379' MD. The 7th BHA consisted of the same Hunting 5/6 8.3 1.0 rev/gal motor and a new
Security MMD54 bit. It drilled to a depth of 18,225' MD and was pulled due to an MWD failure. Finally,
BHA #8 consisted of the same bit, a fresh Hunting motor, and new MWD tools. This bit drilled to a TD of
20,054', making 1,829' in 26 hours.
The lateral was drilled in 9.2 days with 3 trips. Spud to TD was a total of 22 drilling days. The final
closure azimuth was 175.95°, resulting in a closure vertical section of 9,670.07'. The BHL is 9,645.95'
South & 682.59' East from surface location or approx. 316.01' FSL & 2,940.20' FEL SW SE Sec. 9,
T142N, R96W (Figure 2). Salt water drilling fluid was used from the intermediate casing to TD with mud
weights throughout the lateral varying from 9.8-10.1 ppg.

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods:
Geologic supervision of the well was provided by Payzone Consulting, Inc. with two well site geologists.
Brandon Lutz and Bob Troutman drilled the vertical/curve and Kevin Jacks replaced Bob Troutman for the
lateral section. A CanrigTM gas chromatograph was interfaced with a Rigwatch electronic data recorder
system and provided total gas information for viewing around location. Lagged samples were caught in
30' intervals from 8,000'-10,620' with 10' samples collected when landing the curve from 10,620'-10,915'
MD. 100' lagged samples were collected through out the lateral (10,900' -20,054' TD). Cuttings were
examined under a binocular microscope and complete lithologic descriptions are provided in the lithology
document within this evaluation. Two sets of dry cuttings were collected, with one set sent to the North
Dakota Geological Survey Core Library and the second set sent to Jennifer Califf, the project geologist
overseeing operations.
Lithology and Geologic Interpretation:
Geologic evaluation began at 8,000' within the Amsden Formation [Pennsylvanian; Minnelusa Group].
The first top that was used for landing was the Kibbey "Lime" (within the Kibbey Formation)
[Mississippian; Big Snowy Group] which was penetrated at 8,497' TVD (-6,132'). Samples from this
interval were described as:
8510-8540 LIMESTONE: light gray to gray, light gray to brown, mudstone, microcrystalline, blocky, firm to hard, no visible
porosity
The top of the 1st Charles Salt [Mississippian, Madison Group] was penetrated at 8,637' TVD (-6,272').
Within the Charles Formation, the Green Point Anhydrite (GP Anhydrite) was penetrated at 8,905' TVD
(-6,540') and the Base of the Last Charles Salt (BLS) was drilled at 8,990' TVD (-6,625'). Samples from
this interval were described as:
8660-8690 SALT: translucent to occasional clear, rare milky, crystalline, subhedral to anhedral, hard; common;
LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray to gray, light gray to brown, microcrystalline, blocky, firm to hard, anhydrite, no visible
porosity
8900-8930 ANHYDRITE: white to off white, cream, amorphous, soft, earthy texture; ARGILLACEOUS LIMESTONE:
wackestone to mudstone, light gray to gray, trace off white, blocky, friable to firm, crystalline texture, anhydritic in part, no
visible porosity
8960-8990 SALT: translucent to occasional clear, rare milky, crystalline, hard, subhedral to anhedral; ARGILLACEOUS
LIMESTONE: wackestone to mudstone, light gray to gray, trace off white, blocky, friable to firm, crystalline texture,
dolomitic in part, no visible porosity, possible intercrystalline porosity
The top of the Mission Canyon Formation [Mississippian; Madson Group] was drilled at 9,171' TVD
(-6,806'). The prospective Fryburg interval (within the Mission Canyon Formation) was penetrated at
9,340' TVD (-6,975'). The Mission Canyon consisted of interbedded limestone, dolomites, and
anhydrites. Dolomite in the mid to lower Mission Canyon showed fair-moderate intercrystalline porosity to
traces of pinpoint porosity. The samples for this interval were described as:
9170-9200 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray, light gray brown, cream, argillaceous in part, microcrystalline, blocky, firm
to hard, crystalline, occasional earthy texture, no visible porosity; rare ANHYDRITE: off white, massive, amorphous, soft
9230-9260 ANHYDRITE: off white, amorphous, massive, soft; LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, argillaceous
in part, microcrystalline, blocky, friable to firm, earthy to crystalline texture, no visible porosity
9410-9440 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, cream to tan, microcrystalline, friable to firm, earthy texture,
dolomitic in part, argillaceous in part, no visible porosity; trace DOLOMITE: mudstone, light gray, gray, microcrystalline,
friable, crystalline texture, no visible porosity
The argillaceous limestone signifying the top of the Lodgepole Formation [Mississippian; Madison
Group] was penetrated at 9,684' TVD (-7,319') with 798' TVD of consistent lithology described as:
9770-9800 ARGILLACEOUS LIMESTONE: mudstone, mottled off white to buff, tan, light to medium gray, microcrystalline,
firm, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite, no visible porosity
The False Bakken (Carrington Shale) within the Lodgepole Formation was drilled at 10,620' MD;
10,482' TVD (-8,117'). The False Bakken was described as:
10620-10640 SHALE: medium gray to dark gray, firm to hard, blocky, earthy texture, common disseminated pyrite,
calcareous, no visible porosity; ARGILLACEOUS LIMESTONE: as above
The carbonaceous, petroliferous Upper Bakken Shale signifying the top of the Bakken Formation was
penetrated at 10,702' MD; 10,505' TVD (-8,140') and was described as:
10700-10720 SHALE: medium gray to dark gray, firm to hard, blocky, earthy texture, common disseminated pyrite,
calcareous, no visible porosity
The Middle Bakken was penetrated at 10,766' MD; 10,515' TVD (-8,150'). The stratigraphy of the Middle
Bakken consisted of varying thicknesses of siltstone and silty sandstone. (Figure 3) No packstone was
encountered during landing but was penetrated throughout the lateral.
Figure 3. Generalized lithology of the Middle Bakken Member
The Middle Bakken was generally described as:
10760-10780 SILTSTONE: light to medium gray, medium gray brown, friable, sub blocky, calcareous cement, moderately
cemented, common disseminated pyrite, trace intergranular porosity, trace light brown spotty oil stain; SHALE: as above
10850-10880 SILTY SANDSTONE: off white to cream, light gray to gray, light gray brown, very fine grained, friable, sub
rounded to sub angular, calcareous cement, moderately sorted, rare disseminated pyrite, trace intergranular porosity,
possible fracture porosity, trace spotty to even light brown oil stain; SILTSTONE: as above (Figures 4 and 5)
Figure 4 and 5. Wet cutting of the Middle Bakken silty sandstone (left) and hardstreak (right)*
Figure 6. Dry cuttings of the Lower Bakken Shale (close-up, right) *
*All photos: 45x (B. Lutz, Payzone Well site Geologist)
The Lower Bakken Shale, which was encountered at ~12,710' MD, was described as:
11000-11020 SHALE: dark brown, black, blocky, soft to friable, earthy texture, abundant disseminated pyrite, common
nodules pyrite, carbonaceous, petroliferous, no visible porosity (Figure 6)

Kick off point for the curve was established from the offset wells' distance of the "base last salt" marker to
the Middle Bakken target zone. The "base last salt to target" approximation suggested a landing target of
10,519' TVD. The False Bakken was encountered at a TVD of 10,482': 3' low to William Sadowsky 1-4-
9H-142-96, the primary offset. Payzone geologists collaborated with the OXY USA prospect geologist and
decided to change keep the landing target of 10,523' TVD. The wellbore was landed 6' below the UBS
(approximately 10,520' TVD) and just above the into the 7' thick target zone.
LATERAL GEOLOGY: GEOSTEERING
Stratigraphic Relationships and Gamma Signatures:
The Middle Bakken contained three lithologies with distinct gamma signatures. From the top down they
are siltstone, limestone, and silty sandstone (Figures 8, 9). The limestone pinched in at ~16,700' MD. In
places where the limestone is absent, the zone is exchanged with a silty sandstone and siltstone above it
(SR-5). Where the limestone is thick, the siltstone interval thins but is still present (SR-2).
The 7' target window was centered 10.5' below the base of the Upper Bakken Shale (Figure 8). Figure 9
is a geological summary depicting interval thickness and interpreted lateral gamma signature for the
Middle Bakken. The main gamma markers used for geo-steering were the packstone/siltstone interval,
the 50's and 40's API hard streaks in the center/2' above center, and the 70's high and tight gamma ~1.5'
below the center of target. Between these markers, gamma signatures were difficult to discern. The low
swing of gamma typically observed in the center of target is very subtle due to the thin (17-19') Middle
Bakken.

Geosteering and Hardstreaks:
Well developed gamma signatures and trends allowed the well site and Houston geologists to make
steering decisions, thus keeping the wellbore in the 7' targeted interval for the majority of the well (95%).
Figures 8, 9, 10, and 11 depict the main gamma markers as seen on the Wellsite Horizontal log and
Payzone Interpretive Steer dip profiles, respectively.
Siltstone and Limestone (Gamma signature above the target zone)
Silty Sandstone (Gamma signature ~2' above the center of target)
Silty Sandstone (Gamma signature for most of the upper half of zone)
Lower Bakken Shale (Gamma signature ~1' above the Lower Bakken Shale)
Figure 10. Gamma values (0-100 API scale) depicting stratigraphic marker intervals throughout the Middle Bakken.
Due to its proximity, gamma profiles from the William Sadowsky 7-4-9H-142-96 well were used to
anticipate changes in formation dip. This proved futile when the Lower Bakken Shale was encountered @
12,710' MD. We projected the dip to be ~90.30 through this section of the wellbore, but ended up having
to make the dip much steeper (90.70) in order to make the shale strike match with other gamma markers.
This goes to show that no two wells can be precisely correlated. There is too much error in TVD
calculations from the surveys during the lateral. Furthermore, it is absolutely necessary to steer off
gamma markers during the lateral if shale strikes are to be avoided. Payzone geologists' believe that the
thickness of the Middle Bakken in this vicinity is closer to 17' thick when compared to an initial thickness
of 19'.
Two geosteering profiles were maintained by the well site geologists: Inc Sonde Profile and Survey profile
(Figure 11). When drilling 200 ft/hr for the majority of the well, Weatherford's continuous inclination tool
provides an update ~ every 15-20' MD. The survey tool only receives measurements ~ every 96'.
The lateral assemblies did not show a strong tendency to build or fall. The key was anticipating
deflections off of hardstreaks, which were discernable by ROP breaks, low 50's-40's API gamma, and
rapid turnarounds in inclination. The hard streaks were in the center of the target zone and ~2' above the
center of target. If the bit encountered one of these hardstreaks between 1 and 2 degrees above or below
dip, it would deflect strongly and result in an out of control wellbore. If the assembly encountered a
hardstreak at an angle more the 2 degrees above dip, it would penetrate it, refracting through. The closer
the inclination to dip at the bit, the more likely it was to track between the two hardstreaks. This was
accomplished for a few intervals by sliding to control drops or builds just before the bit reached the
hardstreak (Figure 11: 12.500-14,000' MD; 15,500-17,500' MD).
A total depth of 20,054' was reached on January 26, 2015 at 0100h MST. Total depth resulted in 99%
overall exposure within the Middle Bakken Member of the Bakken Formation and 95% within the defined
7' targeted interval (Figure 11).

Hydrocarbons:
During the drilling of the lateral, gas readings were recorded, imported/exported, and analyzed via a
CanrigTM gas detection system. The line was hooked up to the gas sniffer and hard-lined into the base of
the possum belly. This permitted consistent and accurate readings of the gas released from the reservoir.
Background gas ranged from 60-400 units. Connections and gas shows reached as high as 600 units.
There was no observable consistency in gas shows. Gas values were higher in the upper half of the
target zone. Gas could potentially be trapped by the better cemented hard streaks and tight limestone at
the top of the target zone (Figure 12). There is also a noticeable drop in gas above the target zone.

Figure 12. Well profile representing estimated dip value, rop, and total gas for the William Sadowsky 8-4-9H-142-96.
Summary

The X-20 drilling rig successfully drilled a two-section horizontal wellbore within the Middle
Bakken Member of the Bakken Formation at the OXY USA, Inc. William Sadowsky 8-4-9H-142-
96.

A mud program consisting of diesel invert (9.8-10.1 ppg) was used from spud to curve landing
with salt water drilling fluid used from the intermediate casing to 20,054' MD (TD). Salt water mud
(9.8-10.1 ppg) was efficient for maintaining stable down hole conditions and permitted adequate
analysis of gas concentrations in the lateral. Background gas concentrations within the Middle
Bakken ranged from 60-400 units with connections/gas shows as high as 600 units.

Major lithologic/gamma markers used for steering were the limestone/siltstone interval, the two
hard streaks in the upper half of the target zone, and the high and tight gamma in the lower half.
Dip calculations were made based on the wellbore's repeated intersection with these markers.

The lateral was drilled 99% (9,195' MD) in the 17-19' shale to shale zone and 95% (8,823.6' MD)
in the ideal 7' targeted interval. Overall dip of was 0.25°. The key to controlling the assembly
was anticipating deflection off of hard streaks.

Samples from the target consisted of white to off-white, light-dark grey, and brown silty
sandstone. The center of target zone and ~2' above displayed distinct light grey color and fissile
tenacity. It became finer grained and better cemented. These two sections within the target zone
are interpreted to be hard streak off which the wellbore deflected for the duration of the well. Oil
stains were spotty to even and light brown in color.

The William Sadowsky 8-4-9H-142-96 was a drilling effort as measured by gross exposure to the
target. Additionally, knowledge of the geologic complexity in regard to changes in formation dip
will be useful for future wells drilled along this structural contour. The well will be fitted with a 4 ½"
production liner and swell packers in preparation for a fracture stimulation that will determine the
true commercial value of the well.
Respectfully submitted,
Brandon Lutz
Kevin Jacks
Payzone Consulting, Inc.

LITHOLOGY
William Sadowsky 8-4-9H-142-96 Lithology
Rig crews caught samples in 30' intervals from 8,000' to 10,620', 10' intervals from
10,620' to 10,915', and 100' intervals from 10,900' to 20,054' (TD). Formation tops and
lithologic markers have been inserted into the sample descriptions below for reference.
Sample descriptions began in the Amsden Formation. Samples were examined wet and
dry under a binocular microscope. Quantifiers in order of increasing abundance are
trace, rare, occasional, common and abundant. Subsea is delineated as the negative
numbers within the parentheses located next to the measured depth or true vertical depth.
Sample quality was good to excellent. Overall, the samples within the Middle Bakken
target consisted of light-medium grey silty sandstone with common calcite cement and
rare disseminated pyrite. Oil stains were light brown and spotty.
Drilling in Amsden Formation (Pennsylvanian; Minnelusa Group)
8000-8030 SHALE: medium to dark gray, black, soft, blocky, earthy texture, occasional disseminated pyrite, silty to sandy in part;
rare DOLOMITIC LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, microcrystalline, blocky, firm, earthy texture, calcareous in part,
no visible porosity
8030-8060 DOLOMITIC LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, microcrystalline, blocky, firm, earthy texture, calcareous in
part, no visible porosity
8060-8090 SHALE: medium to dark gray, black, soft, blocky, earthy texture, occasional disseminated pyrite, silty to sandy in part;
rare DOLOMITIC LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, microcrystalline, blocky, firm, earthy texture, calcareous in part,
no visible porosity
8090-8120 SHALE: medium to dark gray, black, soft, blocky, earthy texture, occasional disseminated pyrite, silty to sandy in part;
rare DOLOMITIC LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, microcrystalline, blocky, firm, earthy texture, calcareous in part,
no visible porosity
8120-8150 SHALE: medium to dark gray, black, soft, blocky, earthy texture, occasional disseminated pyrite, silty to sandy in part;
rare DOLOMITIC LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, microcrystalline, blocky, firm, earthy texture, calcareous in part,
no visible porosity

Dear Elizabeth:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 25110, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than
the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the
1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 4 & 9 T142NR96W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: OXY may set conductor on permitted wells only. Effective June 1, 2014, a
covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site
beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back
whenever filtration operations are conducted. Due to a stock dam adjacent to the well site, a dike maybe
required surrounding the entire location. OXY USA INC must contact NDIC Field Inspector Nicole
Nelson at 701-290-1527 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum
legal coordinate from the well head is: 9747 S.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Elizabeth S. Bush-Ivie

Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested
that notification be given immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the
Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal
location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are
8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys
must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may
require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
William Sadowsky 8-4-9H-142-96
OXY USA Inc.

COMPASS 5000.1 Build 72
OXY USA INC.
MIDCONTINENT BUSINESS UNIT
WILLISTON DIVISION
GAS CAPTURE PLAN
WILLIAM SADOWSKY NENW 4 PAD
SECTION 4-T142N-R96W
DUNN COUNTY, NORTH DAKOTA
NEW WELLS
WILLIAM SADOWSKY 7-4-9H-142-96
WILLIAM SADOWSKY 8-4-9H-142-96
OCTOBER 13, 2014
Pad
The two wells that will be located on the William Sadowsky NENW 4 Pad are shown in the table
below.
Pipeline Notification
These wells will be connected to Hiland's low pressure gathering system in Dunn County, North
Dakota. Oxy's acreage that comprises the spacing unit (SU) for the William Sadowsky 7-4-9H-
142-96 and William Sadowsky 8-4-9H-142-96 is dedicated to Hiland.
Under terms of the
contract, Hiland is obligated to install the facilities that are required to connect these wells to its
gathering system.
Oxy provides (on a monthly basis) to Hiland a drilling, completion and
estimated first production date for all wells that are scheduled to be drilled in the foreseeable
future. In addition, Oxy and Hiland have conference calls to discuss connection status of wells
and changes to Oxy's drilling and completion schedules when needed.
Gathering System
Gas from this pad will be gathered on Hiland's low pressure WC-Manning Gathering System
and processed at Hiland's Watford City Processing Plant located in Section 6, T151N, R102W,
McKenzie County, North Dakota.
In addition to Hiland, ONEOK owns and operates a low pressure gathering line less than one-
quarter mile north of the pad location.
ONEOK's, along with Hiland's, are shown on the
attached maps.
The production facilities for the William Sadowsky 7-4-9H-142-96 and William Sadowsky 8-4-
9H-142-96 wells will be located south of Hiland's low pressure gathering system. It will require
less than 1,250' of pipe to connect the new wells to Hilands's low pressure gathering system.
Existing Lines
At the terminus of the metering and associated piping at each well's production facilities, the
piping will connect to a 6.625" outside diameter (OD) gathering line. This 6.625" OD gathering
line will be approximately 1,250' of pipeline that will connect the William Sadowsky NENW 4
Pad to a 12.75" OD gathering line. The 12.75" gathering line traverses approximately 5.5 miles
and then connects to the inlet header at Hiland's Manning Compressor Station located in Section
29, T142N, 96W, Dunn County, ND.
The table below shows the estimated capacities and
current flows of the gathering lines connecting this pad.
Hiland stated in a recent meeting that their gathering system in this area had sufficient capacity
to gather gas from wells Oxy currently plans on drilling on the dedicated acreage. Hiland further
stated that the Manning compressor station was designed to allow for the installation of
additional compressors when required as volume increases on the gathering system.
Flowback Strategy
After the fracture treatment, these wells will be flowed through a choke to test production tanks.
Choke size will depend on final shut in pressure post frac and well pressure prior to opening the
choke. The choke will be adjusted up or down based on flowing pressure, liquid rates and sand
returns, to prevent clogging manifold chokes. During flowback, the water chlorides and sand
content will be monitored. When the water chlorides are greater than 100,000 ppm and the
produced fluids contain no sand, the wells will be turned to production facilities. Since the
pipeline is already at the location of the pad and Oxy will have its production facilities
constructed before flowback starts, and gas sales should start as soon as the wells start flowing
through the production facilities. Based on current information, it is our belief the system can
take this gas upon completion of the wells.
The typical well on this pad is expected to initially flow 445 barrels of oil and 200 thousand
cubic feet of gas per day based on Oxy's production type curve of this area. Based on current
drilling and completion plans, these wells will be completed in the same timeframe. For the two
wells, Oxy projects a peak oil rate of 890 barrels and a peak gas rate of 400 thousand cubic feet
per day from the pad. It is anticipated these wells will decline sharply after initial production as
do the majority of horizontal wells in the Williston Basin.
Current Flaring
The table below shows gas produced and sold by Oxy per Gas Production Report - Form 5B that
was filed by Oxy for August 2014 reporting period. The percent sold and percent flared are also
shown in the table.
Flaring Alternative
Wells on this pad will be connected to a pipeline prior to production and Oxy does not expect to
flare gas. Below are three alternatives that Oxy considered from a conceptual standpoint to
reduce the amount of gas flared. More generally, Oxy is continuing to review the possible
impact of implementing one or more of these alternatives as appropriate in our operations.
1) NGL Removal ­ On Lease
Captures highest value components in gas stream
Plants are expensive
Uneconomical to operate when volume declines
Residue gas is still flared
2) Power Generation ­ On Lease
Savings if current generation's fuel supply is diesel
Only a portion of gas is consumed operating the generator, remainder of gas will
be flared
Due to gas quality, high NGL content, preference is to purchase power from the
grid and not operate generation on site
3) Compressed Natural Gas ­ On lease
Well site compressors are required to fill CNG trailers
Large capital outlay for equipment and operating cost, includes trucking of
products, are expensive
No gas would be flared, but might be uneconomical to operate when gas volume
declines

I, William H. Dolinar, Professional Land Surveyor, ND. RLS #6550, hereby certify that (in accordance with a request from Cody Dennison with Oxy USA, Inc., 3239 Highway
22, Dickinson, North Dakota 58601) I and/or personnel under my direction made a survey on the 6th day of August 2014, for the Surface Hole Location and Elevation of platted
well, being located within the NE1/4NW1/4 of Section 4, T142N, R96W of the 5th P.M., Dunn County, State of North Dakota.
Notes: All Azimuths are based on the North line of the Northwest Quarter of Section 4, T142N, R96W of the 5th P.M., being an Azimuth of 269°56'44" using GPS
observations, occupying a WHS control point (5/8" rebar) and having the Location and Elevation derived from an OPUS Solution and GEOID 09. Azimuths shown have been
rotated 1°43'25.54678" West from SPC Grid bearings to Geodetic North, based on convergence angle provided by a conversion using Corpscon.
Project elevations are held on the control point located 173°54'36", 4.48 Feet, from the Northwest Corner of Section 4, T142N, R96W of the 5th P.M. having a NAVD 88
elevation of 2421.44 feet.
Distances shown are Ground Distances using a combined scale factor of 1.000161758.
Location shown here on is not an "ASBUILT" location.
